'Archive Page - http://www.ittoolbox.com//I/siebel-newbie.asp\n\nMike -\n\nIt can\'t be done through EIM, because Account Name is part of the key Siebel\nEIM uses to identify unique records, and Siebel\nwill not let you change that value.\n\nIt could possibly be done via plain old SQL on the backend.  I would\ndefinately test it extensively to make sure nothing\nuntoward happens, though...\n\nGood luck!\n\n"Jahnke, Michael via siebel-newbie-l" wrote:\n\n> Archive Page - http://www.ittoolbox.com//I/siebel-newbie.asp\n>\n> Can anyone tell me if it is possible to mass update Account Names in\nSiebel either through EIM, Workflow, or some other way?\n>\n> Thanks\n>\n> Mike Jahnke\n> SPSS Inc.\n>\n> *Archives: http://www.OpenITx.com/g/siebel-newbie-l.asp\n> *Unsubscribe: mailto:leave-siebel-newbie-l@openitx.com\n> *Terms of Use: http://www.ittoolbox.com/help/termsofuse.htm\n> *Copyright (c) ITtoolbox and message author. 'Archive Page - http://www.ittoolbox.com//I/siebel-newbie.asp\n\nMike -\n\nIt can\'t be done through EIM, because Account Name is part of the key Siebel EIM uses to identify unique records, and Siebel\nwill not let you change that value.\n\nIt could possibly be done via plain old SQL on the backend.  I would definately test it extensively to make sure nothing\nuntoward happens, though...\n\nGood luck!\n\n"Jahnke, Michael via siebel-newbie-l" wrote:\n\n> Archive Page - http://www.ittoolbox.com//I/siebel-newbie.asp\n>\n> Can anyone tell me if it is possible to mass update Account Names in Siebel either through EIM, Workflow, or some other way?\n>\n> Thanks\n>\n> Mike Jahnke\n> SPSS Inc.\n>\n> *Archives: http://www.OpenITx.com/g/siebel-newbie-l.asp\n> *Unsubscribe: mailto:leave-siebel-newbie-l@openitx.com\n> *Terms of Use: http://www.ittoolbox.com/help/termsofuse.htm\n> *Copyright (c) ITtoolbox and message author. 'Gene, it seems to me that we will not have a good clean answer to supporting ABN AMRO for their email application.\n\nOur options are two as I understand from talking to Philip:\n1. We wait for ABN to upgrade all of their Lotus servers to the HTML which may not happen for at least a year since they must upgrade their entire corporate network of Lotus servers, or\n2. We recommend a solution that will convert their current email system to HTML or XML and then render their application. As I understand it at this point, there are two companies that can do the conversion, Plumtree and Info Image. Philip tells me that we have a relationship with info image and he will get info and costing as to what it might take to do the ABN AMRO system and time frames.  We can then go in with credibility and offer the full solution. I would assume that we would be the lead and sub contract info image to do the conversion work.  Alternatively, we could present this opportunity to Accenture who is planning to do a very similar implementation internally (with either Plumtree or info image) and who also have ABN as an active client.  They could prime the who deal and we would be the sub. (Pricing may be an issue to ABN with this solution...Accenture overhead).\n\nThe rendering of the other applications they were talking about from their new portal might be a secondary fall back for us, but I feel if we cant give them a solution to their email requirements, we may not have a second chance in a few months.\n\nInvestment Bankers are ego centric. They want what they want. If we cant meet their most important need (showing off to the other Inv Bkrs in NY that they too have a blackberry pager), then they tend to lose interest and we may lose our sponsor.\n\nWe need to evaluate what Plumtree or info image can do and then determine whether we do it ourselves or decide to include Accenture.\n\nWhat are your thoughts?\n\nRay'

"Ok, I've setup scripts on jakarta and delphi to restart emas if the java exceeds 1 gig (approximately).\n\nIt seems that the only time it totally chokes is when memory gets up that high.  Yes, other errors seem to appear here and there from gog, etc.. on the box but after a minute or so, things clear up, so I used only the java size as an indicator.\n\nRestarting emas without web caused a failed servlet to stay in memory.  I could not resolve this so I went back and spent some time to figure out the proper way to send https pass to the start script.\n\nFor future's sake, the key is this:\n\n1) if you pipe within a pipe (i.e. one script runs another and the main script pipes the results of the child script) the error condition exists where the command line never gets returned.\n\n2) also, if you leave any spaces whatsoever between the echo and the | for piping, problems occur....\n\nanyways, the cron job checks every 15 minutes for a potential restart condition.  If it finds one, it restarts the web (all three [web admin [8888] , web server [80] , https [443])... then it restarts emas in the proper way to finish the job, then emails the results to ops.\n\nI might make some more mods to the scripts, but I think this does it.\n\nscripts:\n/root/domon (parent script)\n/root/emasmon (child script)\n\nCraig"

'This is from one of our classes that connects to lotus:\n\nClass.forName ("sun.jdbc.odbc.JdbcOdbcDriver");\nConnection con = DriverManager.getConnection(URL, odbcProps);\n\nWhere odbcProps is a propert file with these entries:\n\nDSN=MYODBCDSN\nDATABASE=DBDIRECTORY\\\\DATABASENAME.NSF\nSERVER=MYSERVERNAME\n\nAnd URL is DSN preceded by "jdbc:odbc:"\n\nAs someone mentioned, you have to get the NotesSQL ODBC driver to make this\nall work.\n\nAlso, since Lotus Notes doesn\'t allow you to specify a password for your\nNotes ID, you will probably have to run this on a system with a Notes ID\nthat is not password protected.\n\nHope this helps.'
